\authornote{

Correspondence concerning this article should be addressed to Heidi Shi,

\href{mailto:hshi@uoregon.com}{\nolinkurl{hshi@uoregon.com}}}

\abstract{
In recent years, Rstudio and Github have been widely regarded as one of
the essential research tools for social science inquiries
({\textbf{???}}). Previous studies have revealed their significant
methodological impact on disciplines such as psychology, linguistics,
education and so forth (Shi \&Jin, 2017; Lee 2018). This study is an
attempt to solve all the questions listed in Week5 Lab8, one of the most
challenging issues in the history of Fall 2018 EDLD 610
({\textbf{???}}). Through a collaborative approach to lab 8, this study
aims to show that Rstudio and Github are learnable, and sufficient
training is one of the most efficient methods in R language acquisition
({\textbf{???}}).


}

\begin{document}
\maketitle

\section{Methods}\label{methods}

We used methods introduced by Pan and Kádár (2011). Besides we also
adopted the diligent and collaborative approach to Rstudio (see Ahmed,
Arai, and Attia (2001); Kádár and Pan (2011)).

\subsection{Participants}\label{participants}

Cute ducks who are intersted in Rstudio, Female, n=3.

\subsection{Material}\label{material}

Rstudio, an Octopus app called \enquote{GitKraken}, Github.

\subsection{Procedure}\label{procedure}

We compared pre and post-training skills of Rstudio and Github.

\subsection{Data analysis}\label{data-analysis}

We used Kádár and Pan (2011) for all our analyses.

\section{Results}\label{results}
